      "prompt": "## CLI Usage\n\n**IMPORTANT:** There is no `bd` tool in this environment. You must use the `bash` tool to run the `bd` command.\n\n**Do not try to call a tool named `bd` directly.** It does not exist.\n**Do not try to call MCP tools (like `ready`, `create`) directly.** They do not exist.\n\nInstead, use the `bash` tool for all beads operations:\n\n- `bd init [prefix]` - Initialize beads\n- `bd ready --json` - List ready tasks\n- `bd show <id> --json` - Show task details\n- `bd create \"title\" -t bug|feature|task -p 0-4 --json` - Create issue\n- `bd update <id> --status in_progress --json` - Update status\n- `bd close <id> --reason \"message\" --json` - Close issue\n- `bd reopen <id> --json` - Reopen issue\n- `bd dep add <from> <to> --type blocks|discovered-from --json` - Add dependency\n- `bd list --status open --json` - List issues\n- `bd blocked --json` - Show blocked issues\n- `bd stats --json` - Show statistics\n\nIf a tool is not listed above, try `bd <tool> --help`.\n\nAlways use `--json` flag for structured output.\n\n## Subagent Context\n\nYou are called as a subagent. Your **final message** is what gets returned to the calling agent - make it count.\n\n**Your purpose:** Handle both status queries AND autonomous task completion.\n\n**For status/overview requests** (\"what's next\", \"show me blocked work\"):\n- Run the necessary `bd` commands to gather data\n- Process the JSON output internally\n- Return a **concise, human-readable summary** with key information\n- Use tables or lists to organize information clearly\n- Example: \"You have 3 ready tasks (2 P0, 1 P1), 5 in-progress, and 8 blocked by Epic X\"\n\n**For task completion requests** (\"complete ready work\", \"work on issues\"):\n- Find ready work, claim it, execute it, close it\n- Report progress as you work\n- End with a summary of what was accomplished\n\n**Critical:** Do NOT dump raw JSON in your final response. Parse it, summarize it, make it useful.\n\nYou are a task-completion agent for beads. Your goal is to find ready work and complete it autonomously.\n\n# Agent Workflow\n\n1. **Find Ready Work**\n   - Use the `ready` MCP tool to get unblocked tasks\n   - Prefer higher priority tasks (P0 > P1 > P2 > P3 > P4)\n   - If no ready tasks, report completion\n\n2. **Claim the Task**\n   - Use the `show` tool to get full task details\n   - Use the `claim` tool for atomic start-work semantics\n   - Report what you're working on\n\n3. **Execute the Task**\n   - Read the task description carefully\n   - Use available tools to complete the work\n   - Follow best practices from project documentation\n   - Run tests if applicable\n\n4. **Track Discoveries**\n   - If you find bugs, TODOs, or related work:\n     - Use `create` tool to file new issues\n     - Use `dep` tool with `discovered-from` to link them\n   - This maintains context for future work\n\n5. **Complete the Task**\n   - Verify the work is done correctly\n   - Use `close` tool with a clear completion message\n   - Report what was accomplished\n\n6. **Continue**\n   - Check for newly unblocked work with `ready`\n   - Repeat the cycle\n\n# Important Guidelines\n\n- Always claim before working (MCP: `claim`; CLI: `--claim`) and close when done\n- Link discovered work with `discovered-from` dependencies\n- Don't close issues unless work is actually complete\n- If blocked, use `update` to set status to `blocked` and explain why\n- Communicate clearly about progress and blockers\n\n# Available Tools\n\nVia beads MCP server:\n- `ready` - Find unblocked tasks\n- `show` - Get task details\n- `claim` - Atomically claim task for work\n- `update` - Update task status/fields\n- `create` - Create new issues\n- `dep` - Manage dependencies\n- `close` - Complete tasks\n- `blocked` - Check blocked issues\n- `stats` - View project stats\n\nYou are autonomous but should communicate your progress clearly. Start by finding ready work!",

It groups pages by route layouts, modularizes and validates all custom components, ensures DRY practices, and hardens all tests and scripts for compliance and reliability.\n\n## 1. Requirements & Constraints\n\n- **REQ-001**: List and group all Next.js pages in `./app` by route layout: `(auth)`, `(admin)`, `(root)`, and `app/page.tsx`.\n- **REQ-002**: For each group, locate all pages it contains, page-specific components, custom components, DAL, actions, and tests.\n- **REQ-003**: Refactor all components to be fully functional, DRY, and reusable; save dynamic/generic components to `./components/layouts`.\n- **REQ-004**: Validate all reusable components in `./components/layouts` for correctness and reusability.\n- **REQ-005**: Update all tests, helpers, and configurations in `docs/test-context.md` to reflect changes and DRY practices.\n- **REQ-006**: Harden all Vitest and Playwright E2E specs: remove skipped/non-deterministic tests, standardize assertions, and ensure deterministic authenticated scenarios with seeded users.\n- **REQ-007**: Sequentially process all Next.js pages, repeating the above for each.\n- **REQ-008**: As Reviewer Persona, update all custom scripts in `./scripts` for compliance and enhancements.\n- **REQ-009**: As Implementer Persona, update all custom scripts in `./scripts` to be AST-safe and support dry-run functionality.\n- **CON-001**: No use of `any` types; use `unknown` + type guards.\n- **CON-002**: No N+1 queries; all DB access via DAL.\n- **CON-003**: All mutations via Server Actions.\n- **CON-004**: Zero TypeScript errors and lint warnings.\n- **CON-005**: All tests must pass.\n- **PAT-001**: Use DRY and modularization patterns for all components and scripts.\n- **PAT-002**: Use Zod for validation, NextAuth for authentication, and Drizzle ORM for DB access.\n\n## 2. Implementation Steps\n\n### Implementation Phase 1\n\n- GOAL-001: Triage and group all Next.js pages by route layout.\n\n| Task | Description | Completed | Date |\n| --- | --- | --- | --- |\n| TASK-001 | List all Next.js pages in `./app` and group by `(auth)`, `(admin)`, `(root)`, and `app/page.tsx` |  |  |\n| TASK-002 | For each group, enumerate all pages it contains, page-specific components, custom components, DAL, actions, and tests |  |  |\n\n### Implementation Phase 2\n\n- GOAL-002: Refactor and modularize all components, DAL, actions, and tests for each group.\n\n| Task | Description | Completed | Date |\n| --- | --- | --- | --- |\n| TASK-003 | Refactor all group components to be fully functional and DRY |  |  |\n| TASK-004 | Create/Update reusable dynamic/generic components in `./components/layouts` |  |  |\n| TASK-005 | Validate all components in `./components/layouts` for reusability |  |  |\n| TASK-006 | Update all group DAL and actions for compliance and DRY |  |  |\n| TASK-007 | Update all group tests, helpers, and `docs/test-context.md` |  |  |\n\n### Implementation Phase 3\n\n- GOAL-003: Harden all Vitest and Playwright E2E specs.\n\n| Task | Description | Completed | Date |\n| --- | --- | --- | --- |\n| TASK-008 | Remove skipped/non-deterministic tests |  |  |\n| TASK-009 | Standardize all assertions |  |  |\n| TASK-010 | Ensure all authenticated scenarios are deterministic with seeded users |  |  |\n\n### Implementation Phase 4\n\n- GOAL-004: Update and enhance all custom scripts in `./scripts`.\n\n| Task | Description | Completed | Date |\n| --- | --- | --- | --- |\n| TASK-011 | As Reviewer Persona, update all scripts for compliance and enhancements |  |  |\n| TASK-012 | As Implementer Persona, update all scripts to be AST-safe and support dry-run |  |  |\n\n## 3. Alternatives\n\n- **ALT-001**: Refactor pages and components ad hoc without grouping by route layout (rejected for lack of structure and maintainability).\n- **ALT-002**: Only update tests without modularizing components (rejected for not addressing DRY and reusability requirements).\n\n## 4. Dependencies\n\n- **DEP-001**: Next.js 16, TypeScript (strict), Drizzle ORM, PostgreSQL, NextAuth, shadcn/UI, Tailwind CSS v4, Zod, Vitest, Playwright.\n- **DEP-002**: Existing DAL, actions, and test helpers.\n- **DEP-003**: `docs/test-context.md` for test context updates.\n\n## 5. Files\n\n- **FILE-001**: `app/(auth)/**` — All pages, components, DAL, actions, tests under `(auth)` route.\n- **FILE-002**: `app/(admin)/**` — All pages, components, DAL, actions, tests under `(admin)` route.\n- **FILE-003**: `app/(root)/**` — All pages, components, DAL, actions, tests under `(root)` route.\n- **FILE-004**: `app/page.tsx` — Main app page and its dependencies.\n- **FILE-005**: `components/layouts/**` — All reusable dynamic/generic components.\n- **FILE-006**: `dal/**` — All DAL helpers.\n- **FILE-007**: `actions/**` — All Server Actions.\n- **FILE-008**: `tests/**` — All Vitest and Playwright tests.\n- **FILE-009**: `docs/test-context.md` — Test context documentation.\n- **FILE-010**: `scripts/**` — All custom scripts (TypeScript, bash, PowerShell, bat).\n\n## 6. Run in parallel with Tracks A, B, C.\n\n### E1 — Wrap getAllBalances with \"use cache\"\n\n**File:** `actions/plaid.actions.ts`\n\nExtract the loop body of `getAllBalances()` into a new cached helper, or add the `\"use cache\"` directive with `cacheLife` and `cacheTag` directly to the function.\n\n```ts\n// Before\nexport async function getAllBalances(): Promise<{\n  ok: boolean;\n  balances?: Record<string, PlaidBalance[]>;\n  error?: string;\n}> {\n  const session = await auth();\n  if (!session?.user) return { ok: false, error: \"Unauthorized\" };\n\n  const result = await getUserBanks();\n  if (!result.ok || !result.banks)\n    return { ok: false, error: result.error };\n\n  const entries = await Promise.all(\n    result.banks.map(async bank => {\n      const bal = await getBalance({ bankId: bank.id });\n      return [bank.id, bal.ok ? (bal.balances ?? []) : []] as const;\n    })\n  );\n\n  return { ok: true, balances: Object.fromEntries(entries) };\n}\n\n// After — add \"use cache\" block at function top\nexport async function getAllBalances(): Promise<{\n  ok: boolean;\n  balances?: Record<string, PlaidBalance[]>;\n  error?: string;\n}> {\n  \"use cache\";\n  const { cacheLife } =\n    await import(\"next/dist/server/use-cache/cache-life\");\n  const { cacheTag } =\n    await import(\"next/dist/server/use-cache/cache-tag\");\n\n  const session = await auth();\n  if (!session?.user) return { ok: false, error: \"Unauthorized\" };\n\n  cacheLife(\"minutes\");\n  cacheTag(`balances-${session.user.id}`);\n\n  const result = await getUserBanks();\n  if (!result.ok || !result.banks)\n    return { ok: false, error: result.error };\n\n  const entries = await Promise.all(\n    result.banks.map(async bank => {\n      const bal = await getBalance({ bankId: bank.id });\n      return [bank.id, bal.ok ? (bal.balances ?? []) : []] as const;\n    })\n  );\n\n  return { ok: true, balances: Object.fromEntries(entries) };\n}\n```\n\n### E2 — Invalidate balances cache on bank mutations\n\n**File:** `actions/plaid.actions.ts`\n\nIn `exchangePublicToken()` and `removeBank()`, after the mutation succeeds, add:\n\n```ts\nimport { unstable_updateTag as updateTag } from \"next/cache\";\n\n// After successful bank add or remove:\nupdateTag(`balances-${session.user.id}`);\n```\n\n---\n\n## Track F — Test Coverage\n\nRun last — validates all changes from Tracks A–E are type-correct and behaviorally sound.\n\n### F1 — UI store unit tests\n\n**New file:** `tests/unit/stores/ui-store.test.ts`\n\nCover:\n\n- Default state: `sidebarOpen: false`, `activeModal: null`, `drawerOpen: false`\n- `setSidebarOpen(true)` / `setSidebarOpen(false)`\n- `toggleSidebar()` flips the value\n- `openModal(\"transfer\")` sets `activeModal`\n- `closeModal()` sets `activeModal` to `null`\n- `setDrawerOpen(true)` / `toggleDrawer()`\n\n### F2 — Transfer store unit tests\n\n**New file:** `tests/unit/stores/transfer-store.test.ts`\n\nCover:\n\n- Default state: step index 0, empty `formData`, `status: \"idle\"`\n- `nextStep()` advances index; does not exceed last step\n- `prevStep()` decrements index; does not go below 0\n- `goToStep(n)` jumps to step `n`\n- `updateFormData({ amount: \"100\" })` merges into `formData`\n- `setStatus(\"loading\")` updates status\n- `setError(\"msg\")` sets `errorMessage`\n- `setTransferUrl(\"http://...\")` sets `transferUrl`\n- `reset()` returns all state to defaults\n\n### F3 — Filter store unit tests\n\n**New file:** `tests/unit/stores/filter-store.test.ts`\n\nCover:\n\n- Default state: no date range, no category, empty `searchQuery`, `page: 1`, `pageSize: 20`\n- `setDateRange(range)` updates range\n- `setCategory(\"Food\")` updates category\n- `setSearchQuery(\"rent\")` updates query\n- `setPage(3)` updates page\n- `setPageSize(50)` updates pageSize\n- Setting any filter (`setCategory`, `setDateRange`, `setSearchQuery`) resets `page` to 1\n- `reset()` returns all state to defaults\n\n### F4 — Toast store unit tests\n\n**New file:** `tests/unit/stores/toast-store.test.ts`\n\nCover:\n\n- Default state: `toasts: []`\n- `addToast({ title: \"Done\", type: \"success\" })` adds entry with auto-generated id\n- `addToast({ id: \"x\", title: \"Done\" })` uses provided id\n- `removeToast(\"x\")` removes matching toast by id\n- `clearToasts()` empties array\n- Adding multiple toasts produces independent entries\n\n### F5 — Admin E2E spec\n\n**New file:** `tests/e2e/admin.spec.ts`\n\nCover:\n\n- Unauthenticated request to `/admin` redirects to `/sign-in`\n- Non-admin authenticated user redirected away from `/admin`\n- Admin user can load `/admin` and sees the admin dashboard content\n\n---\n\n## Execution Order\n\n```text\nTrack A (quick fixes)    ─┐\nTrack B (dead UI files)  ─┤─► Track C (DAL cleanup) ─► Track D (layout types)\nTrack E (Plaid cache)    ─┘\n\nTrack F (tests) ─► runs last, after all above tracks complete\n```\n\nTracks A, B, C, and E have no inter-dependencies and can be executed in parallel. 1 : undefined,\n  retries: process.env.CI ? 2 : 0,\n  use: {\n    baseURL:\n      process.env.PLAYWRIGHT_BASE_URL ?? \"http://localhost:3000\",\n    screenshot: \"only-on-failure\",\n    video: \"retain-on-failure\",\n    trace: \"on-first-retry\"\n  },\n  reporter: process.env.CI\n    ? [[\"github\"], [\"html\", { open: \"never\" }]]\n    : [[\"html\", { open: \"on-failure\" }]]\n});\n```\n\n### Checklist\n\n- [ ] Add `data-testid` attributes to all interactive elements missing them\n- [ ] Create `tests/e2e/helpers/plaid.ts` with Plaid sandbox flow\n- [ ] Create `tests/e2e/helpers/dwolla.ts` with Dwolla sandbox flow\n- [ ] Add `PLAID_SANDBOX_USERNAME`, `PLAID_SANDBOX_PASSWORD` to `.env.example`\n- [ ] Add `PLAYWRIGHT_BASE_URL` support to `playwright.config.ts`\n- [ ] Set `retries: 2` in CI environment\n- [ ] Add `screenshot`, `video` on-failure config\n- [ ] Add GitHub Actions reporter\n- [ ] Verify `admin.spec.ts` passes after `expect.soft` → `expect` fix\n- [ ] Run `npm run test:ui` — fix all failures\n\n---\n\n## 5. Dockerfile Optimization — Dev vs Production\n\n### Differences\n\n| Concern | Development | Production |\n| --- | --- | --- |\n| Base image | `node:22-alpine` (full Node) | `distroless/nodejs22-debian12:nonroot` |\n| Dev dependencies | Installed | Pruned after build |\n| Source code | Bind-mounted (hot reload) | Copied — standalone output |\n| Build step | None — runs `npm run dev` | `npm run build:standalone` |\n| User | root | `nonroot` UID 65532 |\n| Image size | ~800 MB | ~200 MB |\n| Cache mounts | `--mount=type=cache` | `--mount=type=cache` |\n| Security | `no-new-privileges` | `no-new-privileges` + distroless |\n\n### Production Dockerfile Additions\n\n```dockerfile\n# Pin exact Node version\nFROM node:22.13.1-alpine AS builder\n\n# OCI labels\nLABEL org.opencontainers.image.source=\"https://github.com/YOUR_ORG/banking\"\nLABEL org.opencontainers.image.description=\"Banking App\"\n\n# HEALTHCHECK in image\nHEALTHCHECK --interval=30s --timeout=5s --retries=3 \\\n  CMD wget -qO- http://localhost:3000/api/health || exit 1\n```\n\n### Development Dockerfile Fix\n\n```dockerfile\n# REMOVE unnecessary native build deps (not needed for Next.js)\n# RUN apk add --no-cache python3 make g++ cairo-dev jpeg-dev pango-dev giflib-dev\n```\n\n### Checklist\n\n- [ ] Pin exact Node version in all 3 Dockerfiles\n- [ ] Add OCI `LABEL` metadata to production Dockerfile\n- [ ] Remove unused `apk` native build deps from dev Dockerfile\n- [ ] Add `HEALTHCHECK` instruction to production image\n- [ ] Update entrypoint to `scripts/read-secrets.sh` in production\n- [ ] Document differences in `docs/docker/dev-vs-prod.md`\n\n---\n\n## 8. Environment Variables & Secrets\n\n### Current Files\n\n```text\n.envs/local/.env.local             ← development\n.envs/production/.env.production   ← production template (never commit real values)\n.env.example                       ← public template\n```\n\n### Secrets Strategy\n\nSensitive values use Docker Swarm secrets. Non-sensitive values use `.env` files.\n\n```bash\n# Create Swarm secrets on the server (run once)\necho \"your-encryption-key\" | docker secret create banking_encryption_key -\necho \"your-nextauth-secret\" | docker secret create banking_nextauth_secret -\necho \"postgresql://...\" | docker secret create banking_database_url -\necho \"your-plaid-secret\" | docker secret create banking_plaid_secret -\necho \"your-dwolla-secret\" | docker secret create banking_dwolla_secret -\n```\n\n### Secrets Entrypoint (`scripts/read-secrets.sh`)\n\n```bash\n#!/bin/sh\nset -e\n\nload_secret() {\n  local name=\"$1\"\n  local file_var=\"${name}_FILE\"\n  eval local file_path=\"\\${$file_var:-}\"\n  if [ -f \"$file_path\" ]; then\n    export \"$name=$(cat \"$file_path\")\"\n  fi\n}\n\nload_secret ENCRYPTION_KEY\nload_secret NEXTAUTH_SECRET\nload_secret DATABASE_URL\nload_secret PLAID_SECRET\nload_secret DWOLLA_SECRET\n\nexec \"$@\"\n```\n\n### Stack Secret Config (`stacks/app.stack.yml` excerpt)\n\n```yaml\nservices:\n  app:\n    secrets:\n      - banking_encryption_key\n      - banking_nextauth_secret\n      - banking_database_url\n    environment:\n      ENCRYPTION_KEY_FILE: /run/secrets/banking_encryption_key\n      NEXTAUTH_SECRET_FILE: /run/secrets/banking_nextauth_secret\n      DATABASE_URL_FILE: /run/secrets/banking_database_url\n\nsecrets:\n  banking_encryption_key:\n    external: true\n  banking_nextauth_secret:\n    external: true\n  banking_database_url:\n    external: true\n```\n\n### Checklist\n\n- [ ] Create `scripts/read-secrets.sh`\n- [ ] Update production `Dockerfile` entrypoint to `read-secrets.sh`\n- [ ] Create `stacks/app.stack.yml` with `secrets:` block\n- [ ] Document all vars in `docs/env-vars.md` (sensitive vs plain)\n- [ ] Verify `.envs/production/.env.production` is in `.gitignore`\n- [ ] Update `.env.example` with `_FILE` variants documented\n- [ ] Create `docs/secrets-management.md` with all `docker secret create` commands\n\n---\n\n## 9. Traefik on Docker Swarm\n\n**Target:** Single-node Swarm, self-signed TLS (internal DNS), Prometheus metrics, secured dashboard, HTTP→HTTPS redirect.\n\n### Static Config (`compose/production/traefik/traefik.yml`)\n\n```yaml\nglobal:\n  checkNewVersion: false\n  sendAnonymousUsage: false\n\napi:\n  dashboard: true\n  insecure: false\n\nentryPoints:\n  web:\n    address: \":80\"\n    http:\n      redirections:\n        entryPoint:\n          to: websecure\n          scheme: https\n          permanent: true\n  websecure:\n    address: \":443\"\n    http:\n      tls: {}\n  traefik:\n    address: \":8080\"\n\nmetrics:\n  prometheus:\n    addEntryPointsLabels: true\n    addServicesLabels: true\n    addRoutersLabels: true\n    entryPoint: traefik\n\nlog:\n  level: INFO\n  format: json\n\naccessLog:\n  format: json\n\nproviders:\n  docker:\n    endpoint: \"unix:///var/run/docker.sock\"\n    exposedByDefault: false\n    swarmMode: true\n    network: traefik-public\n  file:\n    directory: /etc/traefik/dynamic\n    watch: true\n```\n\n### Middlewares (`compose/production/traefik/dynamic/middlewares.yml`)\n\n```yaml\nhttp:\n  middlewares:\n    rate-limit:\n      rateLimit:\n        average: 100\n        burst: 50\n    security-headers:\n      headers:\n        stsSeconds: 31536000\n        stsIncludeSubdomains: true\n        forceSTSHeader: true\n        contentTypeNosniff: true\n        browserXssFilter: true\n        referrerPolicy: \"strict-origin-when-cross-origin\"\n    dashboard-auth:\n      basicAuth:\n        usersFile: /run/secrets/traefik_dashboard_users\n    compress:\n      compress: {}\n```\n\n### TLS Config (`compose/production/traefik/dynamic/tls.yml`)\n\n```yaml\ntls:\n  options:\n    default:\n      minVersion: VersionTLS12\n      cipherSuites:\n        - TLS_ECDHE_RSA_WITH_AES_256_GCM_SHA384\n        - TLS_AES_256_GCM_SHA384\n  stores:\n    default:\n      defaultCertificate:\n        certFile: /certs/cert.pem\n        keyFile: /certs/key.pem\n```\n\n### Generate Self-Signed Certs (`scripts/gen-certs.sh`)\n\n```bash\n#!/bin/bash\nset -euo pipefail\nmkdir -p compose/production/traefik/certs\nopenssl req -x509 -nodes -days 3650 -newkey rsa:4096 \\\n  -keyout compose/production/traefik/certs/key.pem \\\n  -out compose/production/traefik/certs/cert.pem \\\n  -subj \"/CN=banking.internal\" \\\n  -addext \"subjectAltName=DNS:banking.internal,DNS:traefik.banking.internal,DNS:grafana.banking.internal,DNS:prometheus.banking.internal\"\necho \"Certs generated in compose/production/traefik/certs/\"\n```\n\n### Init Commands (run once on server)\n\n```bash\ndocker swarm init\ndocker network create --driver overlay --attachable traefik-public\necho \"admin:$(openssl passwd -apr1 'your-password')\" | \\\n  docker secret create traefik_dashboard_users -\necho \"your-grafana-password\" | docker secret create grafana_admin_password -\ndocker stack deploy -c stacks/traefik.stack.yml traefik\ndocker stack deploy -c stacks/app.stack.yml banking\n```\n\n### Checklist\n\n- [ ] Create `compose/production/traefik/traefik.yml`\n- [ ] Create `compose/production/traefik/dynamic/middlewares.yml`\n- [ ] Create `compose/production/traefik/dynamic/tls.yml`\n- [ ] Create `compose/production/traefik/prometheus.yml`\n- [ ] Create `stacks/traefik.stack.yml` (Traefik + Prometheus + Grafana)\n- [ ] Create `stacks/app.stack.yml` with Traefik labels on app service\n- [ ] Create `scripts/gen-certs.sh`\n- [ ] Add `compose/production/traefik/certs/` to `.gitignore`\n- [ ] Add Grafana dashboard JSON for Traefik metrics to `compose/production/traefik/grafana/`\n- [ ] Document Swarm init steps in `docs/traefik/swarm-setup.md`\n\n---\n\n## 10. It covers the pages grouped by layout: (auth) → (admin) → (root) → top-level (Home).\n\nPer repository rules, this plan file is created before making multi-file changes. Implementation will follow the per-page steps defined below. Changes will be made in small commits (one commit per page) and validated with targeted unit tests and type-checking.\n\n## Goals\n\n1. Produce a precise page-by-page inventory (auth → admin → root → top-level) listing files, server/client wrappers, presentational components, server actions, DAL methods, schemas, and tests.\n2. Extract presentational components into `components/layouts/<kebab-name>/index.tsx` where wrappers mix fetching + rendering.\n3. Centralize shared Zod schemas under `lib/schemas/` and import them in both client and server code to avoid drift.\n4. Ensure Server Actions follow the contract: call `auth()` early, validate inputs with Zod, return `Promise<{ ok: boolean; error?: string; ...payload }>` and revalidate caches/tags as needed.\n5. Ensure all DB access occurs only via `dal/*` helpers. Add eager-loading helpers (for example `transactionDal.findByUserIdWithWallets`) to prevent N+1 queries.\n6. Harden tests: use `autoSubmit` + `initial*` patterns for form-based unit tests, use Plaid/Dwolla short-circuit helpers for deterministic E2E and run DB seeding using the seed-runner helpers.\n\n## Scope\n\n- Pages in-scope: `app/(auth)/*`, `app/(admin)/*`, `app/(root)/*` (dashboard, my-wallets, payment-transfer, settings, transaction-history), and `app/page.tsx` (Home) for verification only (Home must remain static/public).\n- Files likely to change: server wrappers, client wrappers, components/layouts additions, `lib/schemas/*`, `dal/*` helpers, and affected tests.\n\n## Risks\n\n- This touches multiple pages and files. Conservative, small commits reduce review overhead and regression risk.\n- Tests may break if schema/types drift — run `npm run type-check` frequently.\n- Seeding and E2E require test flags and mock helpers — follow `docs/test-context.md` and use `npm run db:seed -- --dry-run` before applying changes that require an environment DB.\n\n## Implementation (per-page checklist)\n\nFor each page (repeat):\n\n1. Audit server wrapper\n   - Ensure `auth()` is called first when the page is protected.\n   - Fetch required data in parallel and pass plain data + server action functions into the client wrapper.\n\n2. Audit Server Actions used by the wrapper\n   - Add/ensure Zod validation at top of action with descriptive messages.\n   - Call `auth()` early; return `{ ok: false, error: 'Unauthorized' }` when missing.\n   - Return a stable shape: `Promise<{ ok: boolean; ...payload?; error?: string }>`.\n   - Wrap multi-step writes in `db.transaction(...)` and accept optional `tx` param in DAL writes.\n\n3. Extract presentational UI\n   - If wrapper mixes fetching and rendering, extract a presentational `components/layouts/<kebab-name>/index.tsx` that is props-only and add a unit test next to it.\n\n4. Centralize schemas\n   - Move duplicated Zod schemas to `lib/schemas/<domain>.ts` and import from both client and server.\n\n5. DAL changes\n   - Add/extend eager-loading helpers (e.g., `transactionDal.findByUserIdWithWallets`) to bundle related rows in one query or via batch loads.\n   - Ensure DAL write helpers accept an optional `tx` arg.\n\n6. Tests\n   - Update unit tests to target the extracted components.\n   - Use `autoSubmit` + `initial*` patterns in client wrappers for deterministic tests.\n   - Update E2E to use `tests/e2e/helpers/plaid.mock.ts` and seed runner fixtures. Unknown-but-valid tokens are flagged for manual review rather than auto-added.\n- Destructive Docker operations — mitigated by dry-run default, interactive REMOVE confirmation, and explicit `--force` for non-interactive flows (owner approval required for non-interactive prune).\n- Overwriting helpers or metadata — mitigated by checksum checks, backups (`.bak.<timestamp>`), and audit artifacts.\n\n## Planned Changes\n\n1. CLI: `scripts/mcp-runner.ts` with flags: `--dry-run` (default), `--apply`, `--prune`, `--force`, `--helpers-dir`, `--catalog-path`, `--opencode-path`, `--verbose`, `--dry-run-summary-only`.\n2. Merge servers into an in-memory catalog (include `discoveredVia` and `timestamp`) and present a clear diff on dry-run.\n6. Helper generation: `scripts/mcp-helpers/<server>.ts` — minimal template with provenance header, likely tools list (best-effort), and checksum. On `--apply`: write new helpers, backup and overwrite existing if different, skip identical files.\n7. Update `.opencode/mcp_servers.json` only on `--apply` (backup first). Provide a clear diff in the audit artifact.\n8. Prune: allowed only with `--apply`; present targeted containers and require exact typing of `REMOVE` to proceed. Non-interactive prune requires `--force` plus owner approval (documented), but we will default to interactive-only.\n\n## Validation\n\n- Unit tests (Vitest) for parser, normalization, denylist, and checksum/no-op behavior.\n- Local verification: `node scripts/mcp-runner.ts --dry-run` to preview changes.\n- Post-apply validations (must be run after `--apply`):\n  - `npm run format`\n  - `npm run type-check`\n  - `npm run lint:strict`\n  - `npm run verify:rules`\n  - `npm run test:browser`\n\n## Audit & Artifacts\n\n- On any `--apply`, create an audit artifact `mcp-runner-apply-<timestamp>.json` under `.opencode/mcp-audit/` containing:\n  - Commands executed (gateway, docker ps), truncated outputs, list of files written/backed up/skipped, and the CLI flags used.\n  - Provenance: files read and user decisions.\n\n## Rollback / Mitigation\n\n- Any modified files will have backups with suffix `.bak.<timestamp>` in the same directory. Every line should answer: \"Would an agent likely miss this without help?\" If not, leave it out.\n\nUser-provided focus or constraints (honor these):\n\n## How to investigate\n\nRead the highest-value sources first:\n\n- `README*`, root manifests, workspace config, lockfiles\n- build, test, lint, formatter, typecheck, and codegen config\n- CI workflows and pre-commit / task runner config\n- existing instruction files (`AGENTS.md`, `CLAUDE.md`, `.cursor/rules/`, `.cursorrules`, `.github/copilot-instructions.md`,`.opencode/instructions/*.md`)\n- repo-local OpenCode config such as `.opencode/opencode.json`\n\nIf architecture is still unclear after reading config and docs, inspect a small number of representative code files to find the real entrypoints, package boundaries, and execution flow. Prefer reading the files that explain how the system is wired together over random leaf files.\n\nPrefer executable sources of truth over prose. If docs conflict with config or scripts, trust the executable source and only keep what you can verify.\n\n## What to extract\n\nLook for the highest-signal facts for an agent working in this repo:\n\n- exact developer commands, especially non-obvious ones\n- how to run a single test, a single package, or a focused verification step\n- required command order when it matters, such as `lint -> typecheck -> test`\n- monorepo or multi-package boundaries, ownership of major directories, and the real app/library entrypoints\n- framework or toolchain quirks: generated code, migrations, codegen, build artifacts, special env loading, dev servers, infra deploy flow\n- repo-specific style or workflow conventions that differ from defaults\n- testing quirks: fixtures, integration test prerequisites, snapshot workflows, required services, flaky or expensive suites\n- important constraints from existing instruction files worth preserving\n\nGood `AGENTS.md` content is usually hard-earned context that took reading multiple files to infer.\n\n## Questions\n\nOnly ask the user questions if the repo cannot answer something important. Use the `question` tool for one short batch at most.\n\nGood questions:\n\n- undocumented team conventions\n- branch / PR / release expectations\n- missing setup or test prerequisites that are known but not written down\n\nDo not ask about anything the repo already makes clear.\n\n## Writing rules\n\nInclude only high-signal, repo-specific guidance such as:\n\n- exact commands and shortcuts the agent would otherwise guess wrong\n- architecture notes that are not obvious from filenames\n- conventions that differ from language or framework defaults\n- setup requirements, environment quirks, and operational gotchas\n- references to existing instruction sources that matter\n\nExclude:\n\n- generic software advice\n- long tutorials or exhaustive file trees\n- obvious language conventions\n- speculative claims or anything you could not verify\n- content better stored in another file referenced via `opencode.json` `instructions`\n\nWhen in doubt, omit.\n\nPrefer short sections and bullets. If the repo is simple, keep the file simple. If the repo is large, summarize the few structural facts that actually change how an agent should work.\n\nIf `AGENTS.md` already exists at `C:\\Users\\Alexa\\Desktop\\SandBox\\Banking`, improve it in place rather than rewriting blindly. Preserve verified useful guidance, delete fluff or stale claims, and reconcile it with the current codebase."

org.opencontainers.image.source=\"https://github.com/YOUR_ORG/banking\"\nLABEL org.opencontainers.image.description=\"Banking App\"\n\nHEALTHCHECK --interval=30s --timeout=5s --retries=3 \\\n  CMD Non-sensitive values use `.env` files.\n\n```bash\n# Create Swarm secrets on the server\necho \"your-encryption-key\" | docker secret create banking_encryption_key -\necho \"your-nextauth-secret\" | docker secret create banking_nextauth_secret -\necho \"postgresql://...\" | docker secret create banking_database_url -\n```\n\n### Secrets Entrypoint\n\n```bash\n#!/bin/sh\nset -e\n\nload_secret() {\n  local name=\"$1\"\n  local file_var=\"${name}_FILE\"\n  eval local file_path=\"\\${$file_var:-}\"\n  if [ -f \"$file_path\" ]; then\n    export \"$name=$(cat \"$file_path\")\"\n  fi\n}\n\nload_secret ENCRYPTION_KEY\nload_secret NEXTAUTH_SECRET\nload_secret DATABASE_URL\nload_secret PLAID_SECRET\nload_secret DWOLLA_SECRET\n\nexec \"$@\"\n```\n\n### Checklist\n\n- [ ] Create ports:\n      - \"80:80\"\n      - \"443:443\"\n      - \"8080:8080\" # Dashboard\n    volumes:\n      - /var/run/docker.sock:/var/run/docker.sock:ro\n      - ./compose/production/traefik/traefik.yml:/etc/traefik/traefik.yml:ro\n      - ./compose/production/traefik/dynamic:/etc/traefik/dynamic:ro\n      - ./compose/production/traefik/certs:/certs:ro\n    networks:\n      - traefik-public\n      - app-internal\n    deploy:\n      placement:\n        constraints:\n          - node.role == manager\n```\n\n#### stacks/monitoring.stack.yml      - app-internal\n\n  grafana:\n    image: grafana/grafana:latest\n    ports:\n      - \"3001:3000\"\n    environment:\n      - GF_SECURITY_ADMIN_PASSWORD=admin\n    networks:\n      - app-internal\n```\n\n---\n\n### Scripts Details\n\n#### scripts/read-secrets.sh\n\n```bash\n#!/bin/sh\n# Loads Docker Swarm secrets from _FILE environment variables\n# and exports them as regular environment variables\n\nload_secret() {\n  local name=\"$1\"\n  local file_var=\"${name}_FILE\"\n  eval local file_path=\"\\${$file_var:-}\"\n  if [ -f \"$file_path\" ]; then\n    export \"$name=$(cat \"$file_path\")\"\n  fi\n}\n\nload_secret ENCRYPTION_KEY\nload_secret NEXTAUTH_SECRET\nload_secret DATABASE_URL\nload_secret PLAID_SECRET\nload_secret DWOLLA_SECRET\nload_secret DWOLLA_KEY\n\nexec \"$@\"\n```\n\n#### scripts/gen-certs.sh\n\n```bash\n#!/bin/bash\n# Generates self-signed TLS certificates for Traefik\n\nCERT_DIR=\"compose/production/traefik/certs\"\nmkdir -p \"$CERT_DIR\"\n\n# Generate CA\nopenssl genrsa -out \"$CERT_DIR/ca.key\" 2048\nopenssl req -new -x509 -days 365 -key \"$CERT_DIR/ca.key\" -out \"$CERT_DIR/ca.crt\" -subj \"/CN=Banking CA\"\n\n# Generate server key\nopenssl genrsa -out \"$CERT_DIR/server.key\" 2048\n\n# Generate server cert\nopenssl req -new -key \"$CERT_DIR/server.key\" -out \"$CERT_DIR/server.csr\" -subj \"/CN=banking.example.com\"\nopenssl x509 -req -days 365 -in \"$CERT_DIR/server.csr\" -CA \"$CERT_DIR/ca.crt\" -CAkey \"$CERT_DIR/ca.key\" -CAcreateserial -out \"$CERT_DIR/server.crt\"\n\necho \"Certificates generated in $CERT_DIR\"\n```\n\n#### scripts/server-setup.sh\n\n```bash\n#!/bin/bash\n# Bootstrap Docker Swarm on Hostinger\n\nset -e\n\necho \"Installing Docker...\"\ncurl -fsSL https://get.docker.com | sh\n\necho \"Initializing Docker Swarm...\"\ndocker swarm init --advertise-addr \"$(hostname -I | awk '{print $1}')\"\n\necho \"Creating overlay networks...\"\ndocker network create --driver overlay --attachable traefik-public\ndocker network create --driver overlay --attachable app-internal\n\necho \"Creating directory structure...\"\nmkdir -p /opt/banking/{stacks,compose/production/traefik/certs,scripts}\n\necho \"Docker Swarm initialized successfully!\"\n```\n\n---\n\n### Traefik Configuration Details\n\n####       "template": "# Banking Application Initialization Plan\n\n## Project Overview\n\nThis document provides a comprehensive initialization plan for the Banking application, documenting the current project state, key conventions to maintain, and actionable steps for understanding and working on the project.\n\n## 1. Project State Summary\n\n### Technology Stack\n\n| Component    | Version  | Purpose                           |\n| ------------ | -------- | --------------------------------- |\n| Next.js      | 16.2.2   | App Router, RSC, Cache Components |\n| React        | 19       | UI Framework                      |\n| TypeScript   | 6.0.2    | Type safety with strict mode      |\n| Drizzle ORM  | 0.45.2   | Type-safe SQL queries             |\n| PostgreSQL   | via Neon | Relational database               |\n| NextAuth     | v4.24.13 | Authentication                    |\n| Plaid        | 41.4.0   | Bank account linking              |\n| Dwolla       | 3.4.0    | ACH transfers                     |\n| Zod          | 4.3.6    | Runtime validation                |\n| Playwright   | 1.59.1   | E2E testing                       |\n| Vitest       | 4.1.2    | Unit testing                      |\n| Tailwind CSS | v4       | Styling                           |\n\n### Project Structure\n\n```\nbanking/\n├── app/                    # Next.js App Router pages\n│   ├── (auth)/            # Auth routes (sign-in, sign-up)\n│   ├── (root)/            # Protected routes\n│   ├── (admin)/          # Admin routes\n│   └── api/              # API routes\n├── actions/               # Server Actions\n├── dal/                   # Data Access Layer\n├── database/             # Drizzle schema and config\n├── components/            # UI components\n│   └── ui/               # shadcn/ui components\n├── lib/                   # Shared libraries\n├── scripts/               # Build, seed, verify scripts\n├── tests/                 # Unit and E2E tests\n│   ├── e2e/             # Playwright tests\n│   └── unit/             # Vitest tests\n└── .opencode/            # Agent artifacts\n```\n\n## 2. Key Conventions to Maintain\n\n### Server Actions Pattern\n\nAll mutations must use Server Actions with the following pattern:\n\n```typescript\n\"use server\";\n\nimport { z } from \"zod\";\nimport { userDal } from \"@/dal\";\nimport { revalidatePath } from \"next/cache\";\nimport { auth } from \"@/lib/auth\";\n\nconst CreateUserSchema = z.object({\n  email: z.string().email(),\n  name: z.string().min(1).max(100)\n});\n\nexport async function createUser(\n  input: unknown\n): Promise<{ ok: boolean; error?: string }> {\n  const session = await auth();\n  if (!session?.user) {\n    return { ok: false, error: \"Unauthorized\" };\n  }\n\n  const parsed = CreateUserSchema.safeParse(input);\n  if (!parsed.success) {\n    return { ok: false, error: parsed.error.message };\n  }\n\n  try {\n    await userDal.create(parsed.data);\n    revalidatePath(\"/users\");\n    return { ok: true };\n  } catch {\n    return { ok: false, error: \"Failed to create user\" };\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### Environment Access\n\nAccess environment variables via `app-config.ts` (preferred) or `lib/env.ts`:\n\n```typescript\n// BEST - domain-specific configs\nimport { plaid, dwolla } from \"@/app-config\";\nconst clientId = plaid.PLAID_CLIENT_ID;\n\n// GOOD - backward compat\nimport { env } from \"@/lib/env\";\nconst databaseUrl: string = env.DATABASE_URL;\n\n// BAD - never use process.env directly\nconst databaseUrl = process.env.DATABASE_URL;\n```\n\n### DAL Patterns\n\nUse DAL helpers for all database access to prevent N+1 queries:\n\n```typescript\n// BAD (N+1 pattern)\nconst users = await userDal.findAll();\nfor (const user of users) {\n  user.accounts = await accountDal.findByUserId(user.id);\n}\n\n// GOOD (eager loading)\nconst usersWithAccounts = await userDal.findAllWithAccounts();\n```\n\n### Validation Requirements\n\n- Use Zod for all input validation\n- Include `.describe()` for each field\n- Return consistent shape: `{ ok: boolean; error?: string }`\n\n## 3. Actionable Steps\n\n### For New Contributors\n\n1. Install dependencies:\n\n   ```bash\n   npm install\n   ```\n\n2. Set up environment variables:\n   - Copy `.env.example` to `.env.local`\n   - Fill in required values (Plaid, Dwolla, database)\n\n3. Start development server:\n\n   ```bash\n   npm run dev\n   ```\n\n4. Verify project health:\n   ```bash\n   npm run format\n   npm run type-check\n   npm run lint:strict\n   ```\n\n### For Feature Development\n\n1. Create Server Actions in `actions/` directory\n2. Use DAL helpers in `dal/` for database access\n3. Validate inputs with Zod schemas\n4. Return consistent `{ ok, error? }` shape\n\n### For Testing\n\n1. Run unit tests:\n\n   ```bash\n   npm run test:browser\n   ```\n\n2. Run E2E tests:\n\n   ```bash\n   npm run test:ui\n   ```\n\n3. Run all tests:\n   ```bash\n   npm run test\n   ```\n\n## 4. Pre-PR Validation Checklist\n\nBefore opening a PR, run the following:\n\n- [ ] `npm run format` - Format code\n- [ ] `npm run type-check` - TypeScript validation\n- [ ] `npm run lint:strict` - ESLint with zero warnings\n- [ ] `npm run verify:rules` - Repository policy checks\n\n## 5. Database Commands\n\n```bash\n# Push schema to database\nnpm run db:push\n\n# Generate migrations\nnpm run db:generate\n\n# Run migrations\nnpm run db:migrate\n\n# Seed database\nnpm run db:seed\n\n# Open Drizzle Studio\nnpm run db:studio\n```\n\n## 6. Key Files Reference\n\n| File                   | Purpose                    |\n| ---------------------- | -------------------------- |\n| `AGENTS.md`            | Canonical agent rules      |\n| `app-config.ts`        | Typed environment config   |\n| `lib/auth-options.ts`  | NextAuth configuration     |\n| `lib/auth.ts`          | Server-side session helper |\n| `database/schema.ts`   | Database schema            |\n| `dal/*.dal.ts`         | Data access helpers        |\n| `actions/*.actions.ts` | Server Actions             |\n\n## 7. Common Issues and Solutions\n\n### Port Already in Use\n\nIf port 3000 is in use:\n\n```bash\n# Find and kill process on port 3000\n$pids = Get-NetTCPConnection -LocalPort 3000 -State Listen -ErrorAction SilentlyContinue | Select-Object -ExpandProperty OwningProcess -Unique\nif ($pids) { $pids | ForEach-Object { Stop-Process -Id $_ -Force } }\n```\n\n### Database Connection Issues\n\n- Verify `DATABASE_URL` is set in `.env.local`\n- Check database is running (Neon console, local PostgreSQL)\n- Run `npm run db:push` to sync schema\n\n### Authentication Errors\n\n- Verify `NEXTAUTH_SECRET` is set\n- Check `NEXTAUTH_URL` matches your environment\n- Ensure OAuth credentials are configured in `.env.local`\n\n## 8. Related Plans and Documentation\n\n- Previous work batches: `.opencode/commands/*.plan.md`\n- Cursor plans: `.cursor/plans/*.plan.md`\n- Agent instructions: `.opencode/instructions/`\n- Code philosophy: `.opencode/skills/code-philosophy/`\n\n---\n\n## Status Log\n\n| Date       | Status      | Notes                |\n| ---------- | ----------- | -------------------- |\n| 2026-04-24 | In Progress | Initial plan created |\n\n## Verification\n\n- [x] Tech stack confirmed from package.json\n- [x] Project structure documented\n- [x] Conventions identified from AGENTS.md\n- [ ] Verification commands tested\n- [ ] Database connection validated\n\n---\n\n_Last updated: 2026-04-24_",

    "beads:dep": {
      "description": "Manage dependencies between issues ([command] [from-id] [to-id])",
      "template": "Manage dependencies between beads issues.\n\n## Available Commands\n\n- **add**: Add a dependency between issues\n  - $1: \"add\"\n  - $2: From issue ID\n  - $3: To issue ID\n  - $4: Dependency type (blocks, related, parent-child, discovered-from)\n\n- **remove**: Remove a dependency\n  - $1: \"remove\"\n  - $2: From issue ID\n  - $3: To issue ID\n\n- **tree**: Show dependency tree for an issue\n  - $1: \"tree\"\n  - $2: Issue ID\n  - Flags:\n    - `--reverse`: Show dependent tree (what was discovered from this) instead of dependency tree (what blocks this)\n    - `--format mermaid`: Output as Mermaid.js flowchart (renders in GitHub/GitLab markdown)\n    - `--json`: Output as JSON\n    - `--max-depth N`: Limit tree depth (default: 50)\n    - `--show-all-paths`: Show all paths (no deduplication for diamond dependencies)\n\n- **cycles**: Detect dependency cycles\n\n## Dependency Types\n\n- **blocks**: Hard blocker (from blocks to) - affects ready queue\n- **related**: Soft relationship - for context only\n- **parent-child**: Epic/subtask relationship\n- **discovered-from**: Track issues found during work\n\n## Mermaid Format\n\nThe `--format mermaid` option outputs the dependency tree as a Mermaid.js flowchart:\n\n**Example:**\n```bash\nbd dep tree bd-1 --format mermaid\n```\n\nOutput can be embedded in markdown:\n\n````markdown\n```mermaid\nflowchart TD\n  bd-1[\"◧ bd-1: Main task\"]\n  bd-2[\"☑ bd-2: Subtask\"]\n\n  bd-1 --> bd-2\n```\n````\n\n**Status Indicators:**\n\nEach node includes a symbol indicator for quick visual status identification:\n\n- ☐ **Open** - Not started yet (empty checkbox)\n- ◧ **In Progress** - Currently being worked on (half-filled box)\n- ⚠ **Blocked** - Waiting on something (warning sign)\n- ☑ **Closed** - Completed! (checked checkbox)\n\nThe diagram colors are determined by your Mermaid theme (default, dark, forest, neutral, or base). Mermaid diagrams render natively in GitHub, GitLab, VSCode markdown preview, and can be imported to Miro.\n\n## Examples\n\n- `bd dep add bd-10 bd-20 --type blocks`: bd-10 depends on bd-20 (bd-20 blocks bd-10)\n- `bd dep tree bd-20`: Show what blocks bd-20 (dependency tree going UP)\n- `bd dep tree bd-1 --reverse`: Show what was discovered from bd-1 (dependent tree going DOWN)\n- `bd dep tree bd-1 --reverse --max-depth 3`: Show discovery tree with depth limit\n- `bd dep tree bd-20 --format mermaid > tree.md`: Generate Mermaid diagram for documentation\n- `bd dep cycles`: Check for circular dependencies\n\n## Reverse Mode: Discovery Trees\n\nThe `--reverse` flag inverts the tree direction to show **dependents** instead of **dependencies**:\n\n**Normal mode** (`bd dep tree ISSUE`):\n- Shows what blocks you (dependency tree)\n- Answers: \"What must I complete before I can work on this?\"\n- Tree flows **UP** toward prerequisites\n\n**Reverse mode** (`bd dep tree ISSUE --reverse`):\n- Shows what was discovered from you (dependent tree)\n- Answers: \"What work was discovered while working on this?\"\n- Tree flows **DOWN** from goal to discovered tasks\n- Perfect for visualizing work breakdown and discovery chains\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Document project evolution and how work expanded from initial goal\n- Share \"how we got here\" context with stakeholders\n- Visualize work breakdown structure from epics\n- Track discovery chains (what led to what)\n- Show yak shaving journeys in retrospectives"
    },

    "beads:list": {
      "description": "List issues with optional filters ([--status] [--priority] [--type] [--assignee] [--label])",
      "template": "List beads issues with optional filtering.\n\n## Basic Filters\n\n- **--status, -s**: Filter by status (open, in_progress, blocked, closed)\n- **--priority, -p**: Filter by priority (0-4: 0=critical, 1=high, 2=medium, 3=low, 4=backlog)\n- **--type, -t**: Filter by type (bug, feature, task, epic, chore, decision)\n- **--assignee, -a**: Filter by assignee\n- **--label, -l**: Filter by labels (comma-separated, must have ALL labels)\n- **--label-any**: Filter by labels (OR semantics, must have AT LEAST ONE)\n- **--title**: Filter by title text (case-insensitive substring match)\n- **--limit, -n**: Limit number of results\n\n## Advanced Filters\n\n### Pattern Matching\n- **--title-contains**: Search for text in title (case-insensitive)\n- **--desc-contains**: Search for text in description (case-insensitive)\n- **--notes-contains**: Search for text in notes (case-insensitive)\n\n### Date Ranges\n- **--created-after**: Issues created after date (YYYY-MM-DD or ISO 8601)\n- **--created-before**: Issues created before date\n- **--updated-after**: Issues updated after date\n- **--updated-before**: Issues updated before date\n- **--closed-after**: Issues closed after date\n- **--closed-before**: Issues closed before date\n\n### Priority Range\n- **--priority-min**: Minimum priority (inclusive)\n- **--priority-max**: Maximum priority (inclusive)\n\n### Empty/Null Checks\n- **--empty-description**: Find issues with no description\n- **--no-assignee**: Find unassigned issues\n- **--no-labels**: Find issues with no labels\n\n## Examples\n\n### Basic Usage\n- `bd list --status open --priority 1`: High priority open issues\n- `bd list --type bug --assignee alice`: Alice's assigned bugs\n- `bd list --label backend,needs-review`: Backend issues needing review\n- `bd list --title \"auth\"`: Issues with \"auth\" in the title\n\n### Advanced Usage\n- `bd list --title-contains \"auth\" --status open`: Search open issues for auth-related work\n- `bd list --priority-min 0 --priority-max 1`: Critical and high priority issues only\n- `bd list --created-after 2025-01-01 --status open`: Recent open issues\n- `bd list --empty-description --status open`: Open issues missing descriptions\n- `bd list --no-assignee --priority 1`: High priority unassigned work\n- `bd list --desc-contains \"TODO\" --notes-contains \"review\"`: Find items needing attention\n\n## Output Formats\n\n- Default: Human-readable table\n- `--json`: JSON format for scripting\n- `--format digraph`: Graph format for golang.org/x/tools/cmd/digraph\n- `--format dot`: Graphviz DOT format"
    },

    "beads:search": {
      "description": "Search issues by text query (<query> [--status] [--label] [--assignee])",
      "template": "Search issues across title, description, and ID with a simple text query.\n\n**Note:** The `search` command is optimized for quick text searches and uses less context than `list` when accessed via MCP. For advanced filtering options, use `bd list`.\n\n## Basic Usage\n\n```bash\nbd search \"authentication bug\"\nbd search login --status open\nbd search database --label backend\nbd search \"bd-5q\"  # Search by partial issue ID\n```\n\n## How It Works\n\nThe search command finds issues where your query appears in **any** of:\n- Issue title\n- Issue description\n- Issue ID (supports partial matching)\n\nUnlike `bd list`, which requires you to specify which field to search, `bd search` automatically searches all text fields, making it faster and more intuitive for exploratory searches.\n\n## Filters\n\n- **--status, -s**: Filter by status (open, in_progress, blocked, closed)\n- **--assignee, -a**: Filter by assignee\n- **--type, -t**: Filter by type (bug, feature, task, epic, chore, decision)\n- **--label, -l**: Filter by labels (must have ALL specified labels)\n- **--label-any**: Filter by labels (must have AT LEAST ONE)\n- **--limit, -n**: Limit number of results (default: 50)\n- **--sort**: Sort by field: priority, created, updated, closed, status, id, title, type, assignee\n- **--reverse, -r**: Reverse sort order\n- **--long**: Show detailed multi-line output for each issue\n- **--json**: Output results in JSON format\n\n## Examples\n\n### Basic Search\n```bash\n# Find all issues mentioning \"auth\" or \"authentication\"\nbd search auth\n\n# Search for performance issues\nbd search performance --status open\n\n# Find database-related bugs\nbd search database --type bug\n```\n\n### Filtered Search\n```bash\n# Find open backend issues about login\nbd search login --status open --label backend\n\n# Search Alice's tasks for \"refactor\"\nbd search refactor --assignee alice --type task\n\n# Find recent bugs (limited to 10 results)\nbd search bug --status open --limit 10\n```\n\n### Sorted Output\n```bash\n# Search bugs sorted by priority (P0 first)\nbd search bug --sort priority\n\n# Search features sorted by most recently updated\nbd search feature --sort updated\n\n# Search issues sorted by priority, lowest first\nbd search refactor --sort priority --reverse\n```\n\n### JSON Output\n```bash\n# Get JSON results for programmatic use\nbd search \"api error\" --json\n\n# Use with jq for advanced filtering\nbd search memory --json | jq '.[] | select(.priority <= 1)'\n```\n\n## Comparison with bd list\n\n| Command | Best For | Default Limit | Context Usage |\n|---------|----------|---------------|---------------|\n| `bd search` | Quick text searches, exploratory queries | 50 | Low (efficient for LLMs) |\n| `bd list` | Advanced filtering, precise queries | None | High (all results) |\n\n**When to use `bd search`:**\n- You want to find issues quickly by keyword\n- You're exploring the issue database\n- You're using an LLM/MCP and want to minimize context usage\n\n**When to use `bd list`:**\n- You need advanced filters (date ranges, priority ranges, etc.)\n- You want all results without a limit\n- You need special output formats (digraph, dot)"
    },

    "beads:workflow": {
      "description": "Show the AI-supervised issue workflow guide",
      "template": "Display the beads workflow for AI agents and developers.\n\n# Beads Workflow\n\nBeads is an issue tracker designed for AI-supervised coding workflows. Here's how to use it effectively:\n\n## 1. Find Ready Work\nUse `/beads:ready` or the `ready` MCP tool to see tasks with no blockers.\n\n## 2. Claim Your Task\nClaim the issue atomically (assignee + `in_progress` in one step):\n- Via command: `/beads:update <id> --claim`\n- Via MCP tool: `claim` with `issue_id: \"<id>\"`\n\n## 3. Work on It\nImplement, test, and document the feature or fix.\n\n## 4. Discover New Work\nAs you work, you'll often find bugs, TODOs, or related work:\n- Create issues: `/beads:create` or `create` MCP tool\n- Link them: Use `dep` MCP tool with `type: \"discovered-from\"`\n- This maintains context and work history\n\n## 5. Complete the Task\nClose the issue when done:\n- Via command: `/beads:close <id> \"Completed: <summary>\"`\n- Via MCP tool: `close` with reason\n\n## 6. Check What's Unblocked\nAfter closing, check if other work became ready:\n- Use `/beads:ready` to see newly unblocked tasks\n- Start the cycle again\n\n## Tips\n- **Priority levels**: 0=critical, 1=high, 2=medium, 3=low, 4=backlog\n- **Issue types**: bug, feature, task, epic, chore\n- **Dependencies**: Use `blocks` for hard dependencies, `related` for soft links\n- **Auto-sync**: Changes are stored in Dolt and synced via `bd dolt push` / `bd dolt pull`\n\n## Available Commands\n- `/beads:ready` - Find unblocked work\n- `/beads:create` - Create new issue\n- `/beads:show` - Show issue details\n- `/beads:update` - Update issue\n- `/beads:close` - Close issue\n- `/beads:workflow` - Show this guide (you are here!)\n\n## MCP Tools Available\nUse these via the beads MCP server:\n- `ready`, `list`, `show`, `create`, `claim`, `update`, `close`\n- `dep` (manage dependencies), `blocked`, `stats`\n- `init` (initialize bd in a project)\n\nFor more details, see the beads README at: https://github.com/steveyegge/beads"
